4 SYNOPSIS:
6 expenses of the executive, legislative, and judicial
7 agencies of the State, for other functions of
8 government, for debt service, and for capital outlay
9 for the fiscal year ending September 30, 2027.
10
11
12 A BILL
13 TO BE ENTITLED
14 AN ACT
15
16 To make appropriations for the ordinary expenses of the
17 executive, legislative, and judicial agencies of the State,
18 for other functions of government, for debt service, and for
19 capital outlay for the fiscal year ending September 30, 2027.
20 BE IT ENACTED BY THE LEGISLATURE OF ALABAMA:
21 Section 1. The monies in Section 3 are appropriated
22 from the named funds for the 2027 fiscal year to the state
23 agencies indicated, as the amounts to be used to pay the
24 expenditures of the named agencies, and are in lieu of all
25 monies appropriated for these purposes in other sections of
26 the Alabama Statutes.
27 For the purpose of this act, the amounts herein for
Page 1
For the purpose of this act, the amounts herein for
SB146 INTRODUCED
28 expenditures are listed by programmatic area and the totals
29 for all programs are shown by the source of funds. It is
30 intended that only the herein named funds be appropriated in
31 the amounts specified to the named agencies and that the
32 following definitions shall be applicable.
33 "Total" shall mean the aggregate total appropriation of
34 all funding sources.
35 "Program" shall mean specific governmental services
36 required to achieve a specific objective. A program shall be
37 directed to meeting the need of an identified clientele, or
38 group of recipients or beneficiaries, and shall be expended
39 only for such purposes.
40 "Capital Outlay" shall mean expenditures which result
41 in the acquisition and/or addition to items, such as land or
42 buildings, which have an appreciable and calculable period of
43 usefulness in excess of one year, and shall be expended only
44 for such purposes.
45 "Debt Service" shall mean an expenditure for the
46 payment of interest and principal on bonded debt obligations
47 of the State, and shall be expended only for such purposes.
48 "Federal and Local Funds" shall mean all gifts, grants,
49 contributions, or entitlements, including grants by the
50 Congress of the United States, municipalities or counties.
51 Section 2. (a) There is hereby appropriated the amounts
52 set forth herein for the ordinary expenses of the executive,
53 legislative, and judicial agencies of the State, for other
54 functions of government, for debt service, and for capital
Page 2
functions of government, for debt service, and for capital
SB146 INTRODUCED
55 outlay for the fiscal year ending September 30, 2027, to be
56 paid out of any monies hereinafter specified, from such other
57 funds and accounts as may be designated, or so much thereof as
58 may be necessary, and the total amount to be expended for the
59 items for which the appropriation is herein made shall not
60 exceed the amount provided therefor, except as provided in the
61 Budget Management Act of 1976, Sections 41-19-1 through
62 41-19-12, Code of Alabama 1975. Provided, however, that
63 regardless of the ending date of any pay period which has been
64 or may be established by the Legislature for the payment of
65 salaries of state employees, the entire payment due shall be
66 made from the fiscal year's appropriation in which the pay
67 date falls.
68 (b) All appropriations made in Section 3 shall be at
69 the program level. Any directed expenditure of funds below a
70 program shall be from funds appropriated for the program.
Page 3
program shall be from funds appropriated for the program.

SB146 INTRODUCED
State General
Fund Other Funds Total
296 In addition to the above appropriation herein made, there is hereby appropriated for
297 each additional retail and wholesale store that is relocated or put into operation
298 during the fiscal year, an amount equal to the sum required to install and operate a
299 comparable store in operation by said Board. There is further appropriated to the
300 Alabama Alcoholic Beverage Control Board, after provision has been made for the
301 other expenditures herein authorized, such sums as are or may be necessary to
302 purchase the alcoholic beverages which are essential to maintain adequate stocks and
303 inventory for an economic and successful sales operation. In addition to the above
304 appropriation, it is further provided that, in the event any county or municipality
305 of the state shall, during the fiscal period covered by this appropriation by proper
306 referendum, authorize the legal sale of malt and brewed beverages within such county
307 or municipality there is further appropriated, in addition to the amount herein set
308 out, an amount comparable to that expended during the prior fiscal year for beer and
309 license tax supervision within counties or municipalities of similar size and
310 population. Provided further, that the amount appropriated herein shall be reduced
311 in like manner in the event any county or municipality wherein malt and brewed
312 beverages are now authorized by law to be sold shall, during the fiscal period
313 covered by this appropriation by proper referendum, declare unlawful the sale in
314 such county or municipality of such malt or brewed beverages. Notwithstanding any
315 other laws to the contrary, all revenue generated from bailment fees shall remain
316 with the Board to be used for its operations.

1255 61. Health, Department of Public:
1256 (a) Administrative Services 18,191,907 33,391,469 51,583,376
1257 Program
1258 (1) Office of Primary Care and Rural 500,000
1259 Health
1260 For award payments to licensed physicians or nurse practitioners who agree to practice
1261 full-time in primary care in a medically underserved rural area for an agreed upon number of
1262 years. No payment shall be allowed for a physician or nurse practitioner who has practiced
1263 within three years of October 1, 2026, in a primary care service area with a deficit, or
1264 surplus of less than 2.0 primary-care physicians, as shown by the most-recent Status Report of
1265 the Alabama Primary Care Physician Workforce from the Office for Family Health Education &
1266 Research at the UAB Huntsville Regional Medical Campus. The Office of Primary Care and Rural
1267 Health may pay an eligible physician or nurse practitioner as much as $50,000 a year for each
1268 year of service, in a medically underserved rural area, agreed to by contract by the physician
1269 or nurse practitioner, but any payment shall be for no more than three years. Contracts shall
1270 set out refund and penalty requirements for failure by a physician or nurse practitioner to
1271 meet the contract terms. A medically underserved rural area as determined by the Office shall
1272 be: (1.) in a rural primary care service area with a deficit of primary-care physicians as
1273 shown by the most recent Status Report of the Alabama Primary Care Physician Workforce, and
1274 (2.) in a county in which no more than two physicians have worked or are scheduled to be
1275 working within 12 months to repay a loan awarded by the Alabama Board of Medical Scholarship
1276 Awards. The Office shall file a report with the Chairs of the Senate Committee on Finance and
1277 Taxation-General Fund and the House Ways and Means-General Fund Committee, the Legislative
1278 Fiscal Officer and the Finance Director by October 15, 2027, on how the money was spent in
1279 fiscal year 2027 and the names of participants and where they agreed to practice or were
1280 practicing in return for payments from the Office.

1314 To award matching grants for ambulances for emergency medical services operating in rural
1315 counties. The Office may consider requests for matching grants to buy an ambulance,
1316 rapid-response vehicle, or cardiac monitor or other durable medical equipment to be placed in
1317 an ambulance or rapid-response vehicle, from a county, city, hospital, or ambulance service.
1318 The Office may award a grant equal to no more than 75 percent of the cost of the ambulance,
1319 rapid-response vehicle, or equipment, the percentage depending on the financial resources of
1320 the applicant and the need for the vehicle or equipment as judged by officials with the state’s
1321 regional emergency medical services offices. Preference shall be given to grants for an
1322 ambulance or rapid-response vehicle that would be based in a county with two or fewer
1323 ambulances. The Office shall file a report with the Chairs of the Senate Committee on Finance

1756 84. Medicaid Agency, Alabama:
1757 (a) Medical Assistance through 1,179,054,000 9,338,373,438 10,517,427,438
1758 Medicaid Program
1759 The Medicaid Agency shall make every effort to maintain level funding for the
1760 adult prosthetic and orthotic program in fiscal year 2027. Any requirements
1761 for prior authorization of antipsychotic drugs will be for the limited purpose
1762 of managing off-label utilization. The Medicaid Agency shall make every effort
1763 to provide access for medications prescribed in accordance with FDA approved
1764 indications for mental illness and HIV/AIDS. The Alabama Medicaid Agency shall
1765 not pay for a generic drug that is more expensive than its brand name drug,
1766 net of rebates. The Alabama Medicaid Agency shall continue to fund and support
1767 the PACE program in accordance with written agreements.

2455 Total Revenue, Department of 363,000 229,166,353 229,529,353
2456 The amounts hereinabove appropriated for the cost of maintenance and operations of
2457 the Department of Revenue are in lieu of any other statutory provisions for the
2458 payment of the cost of operating said Department for collections of the taxes as
2459 authorized by law. Provided, however, in addition to the amount hereinabove
2460 appropriated, there is hereby appropriated to the Department of Revenue all sums
2461 allowed the Department of Revenue by acts of the Legislature as a charge for the
2462 collection of taxes or licenses. The Revenue Department shall not be limited in any
2463 way whatsoever in its ability to utilize or spend its full appropriation and all
2464 sums allowed to the Department of Revenue by acts of the Legislature as a charge for
2465 the collection of taxes or licenses. It is the intent of the Legislature that the
2466 Department of Revenue utilize the appropriations made to it in this act to: (1)
2467 significantly reduce the amount of delinquent taxes owed to the state; (2) employ
2468 sufficient examiners and audit personnel to ensure that taxes owed to the state are
2469 collected accurately and timely; and (3) update its personal computers and related
2470 equipment to become more efficient in the collection of taxes owed to the state.
2471 During Fiscal Year 2027, the Department shall report semi-annually to the Chairs of
2472 the House Ways and Means-General Fund Committee, Senate Finance and Taxation-General
2473 Fund Committee, and the Legislative Fiscal Officer on all actions taken by the
2474 Department in furtherance of these goals. The reports shall include, but not be
2475 limited to: (1) the number and amount of delinquent taxes collected during the
2476 quarter and the number and amounts of delinquent taxes outstanding as of the end of
2477 the quarter; (2) the number of additional examiners and audit personnel employed
2478 during the quarter (not including examiners and audit personnel employed to replace
2479 personnel that retire or otherwise leave state service); and (3) the number of new
2480 personal computers and related equipment put into use during the quarter.

2528 The Alabama SenioRx program shall provide assistance obtaining prescription
2529 medications and shall be expanded to allow comprehensive benefits screening
2530 and application assistance through an Area Agency on Aging designated by the
2531 Department as an Aging and Disability Resource Center (ADRC). It is the intent
2532 of the Legislature that applicants apply through local Area Agencies on Aging
2533 and their provider networks to ensure services are maximized and that
2534 paperwork and inconvenience to the clients are minimized to receive access to
2535 local and public benefits and prescription assistance. The Department of
2536 Senior Services shall report semi-annually to the Chairs of the House Ways and
2537 Means-General Fund Committee and the Senate Finance and Taxation-General Fund
2538 Committee, the Governor, the Director of Finance, and the Legislative Fiscal
2539 Officer. The reports shall include the number of clients served by an ADRC,
2540 the number of unduplicated SenioRx participants, the number of prescriptions
2541 filled, and the estimated value of the drugs provided.

3206 Section 4. In addition to the amounts otherwise

3208 the several funds in the State Treasury, except the Education
3209 Trust Fund, and in the same proportion as the salaries of the
3210 several State officials and employees are paid, such
3211 additional amounts as may be necessary to pay for a two
3212 percent (2%) salary increase enacted in the 2026 Regular
3213 Session. The additional amounts appropriated in this section
3214 from the State General Fund shall not exceed $16,000,000 for
3215 the fiscal year ending September 30, 2027. The Director of
3216 Finance shall ensure that first priority shall be given to all
3217 State General Fund payrolls, including the payroll of the
3218 Legislature. State agencies shall receive additional
3219 allocations from the appropriation made in this section from

3221 salaries paid from the State General Fund by two percent. The
3222 remainder of this appropriation from the State General Fund
3223 may be allotted by the Director of Finance to those agencies
3224 which receive transfers from the State General Fund.

3324 state agencies cooperate with the Examiners of Public Accounts
3325 to provide the information necessary to conduct recovery
3326 audits as provided for in Section 41-5A-6, Code of Alabama
3327 1975.

3331 other costs relating to said court order, funds are hereby

3333 commission from the appropriate fund or funds of such
3334 department, board, bureau, or commission in the amount
3335 necessary to satisfy that court order. Such appropriations are
3336 in addition to any other appropriation heretofore or hereafter

3343 90-556, and Act 91-572 are hereby appropriated to the

3346 Revenue Sharing Investments under the State and Local Fiscal
3347 Assistance Act of 1972, as amended, Public Law 92-512, 92nd
3348 Congress, together with any accruals or reversions thereon are
3349 hereby appropriated to the State General Fund.
3350 Section 16. Upon certification to the Director of
3351 Finance by the Director of the Alabama Emergency Management
3352 Agency that a disaster related expenditure was necessary to
3353 ensure life safety and incident stabilization for the State of
3354 Alabama as a result of an all hazard event, to include natural
3355 and man-made hazards, funds are hereby appropriated to the
3356 affected department from the State General Fund or any other
3357 fund necessary to satisfy the expenditure. Such appropriations
3358 are in addition to any other appropriation heretofore and
3359 hereafter made in this appropriation act. Such appropriations
3360 are conditioned upon the availability of funds and a

3362 appropriations are not available for the disaster related

3404 appropriated from the State General Fund in the same
3405 proportion as the salaries of the several State officials and

3408 appropriated in this section from the State General Fund shall
3409 not exceed $18,000,000 for the fiscal year ending September
3410 30, 2027. The Director of Finance shall ensure first priority
3411 shall be given to all State General Fund payrolls, including

3452 Section 25. If any section, paragraph, sentence,
3453 clause, provision, or portion of this act or all or any
3454 portion of any appropriations herein made be held

3460 Section 26. All laws or parts of laws, general,
3461 special, private, or local that are in conflict with or
3462 inconsistent with the provisions of this act are hereby
3463 expressly repealed.
3464 Section 27. Each agency of the state funded through
3465 the provisions of this act shall provide an equal opportunity
3466 for employment and business opportunities for all citizens of

4 SYNOPSIS:
5 This bill makes appropriations for the ordinary
6 expenses of the executive, legislative, and judicial
7 agencies of the State, for other functions of
8 government, for debt service, and for capital outlay
9 for the fiscal year ending September 30, 2027.
10
11
12 A BILL
13 TO BE ENTITLED
14 AN ACT
15
16 To make appropriations for the ordinary expenses of the
17 executive, legislative, and judicial agencies of the State,
18 for other functions of government, for debt service, and for
19 capital outlay for the fiscal year ending September 30, 2027.
20 BE IT ENACTED BY THE LEGISLATURE OF ALABAMA:
21 Section 1. The monies in Section 3 are appropriated
22 from the named funds for the 2027 fiscal year to the state
23 agencies indicated, as the amounts to be used to pay the
24 expenditures of the named agencies, and are in lieu of all
25 monies appropriated for these purposes in other sections of
26 the Alabama Statutes.
27 For the purpose of this act, the amounts herein for
Page 1

For the purpose of this act, the amounts herein for
SB146 INTRODUCED
28 expenditures are listed by programmatic area and the totals
29 for all programs are shown by the source of funds. It is
30 intended that only the herein named funds be appropriated in
31 the amounts specified to the named agencies and that the
32 following definitions shall be applicable.
33 "Total" shall mean the aggregate total appropriation of
34 all funding sources.
35 "Program" shall mean specific governmental services
36 required to achieve a specific objective. A program shall be
37 directed to meeting the need of an identified clientele, or
38 group of recipients or beneficiaries, and shall be expended
39 only for such purposes.
40 "Capital Outlay" shall mean expenditures which result
41 in the acquisition and/or addition to items, such as land or
42 buildings, which have an appreciable and calculable period of
43 usefulness in excess of one year, and shall be expended only
44 for such purposes.
45 "Debt Service" shall mean an expenditure for the
46 payment of interest and principal on bonded debt obligations
47 of the State, and shall be expended only for such purposes.
48 "Federal and Local Funds" shall mean all gifts, grants,
49 contributions, or entitlements, including grants by the
50 Congress of the United States, municipalities or counties.
51 Section 2. (a) There is hereby appropriated the amounts
52 set forth herein for the ordinary expenses of the executive,
53 legislative, and judicial agencies of the State, for other
54 functions of government, for debt service, and for capital
Page 2

functions of government, for debt service, and for capital
SB146 INTRODUCED
55 outlay for the fiscal year ending September 30, 2027, to be
56 paid out of any monies hereinafter specified, from such other
57 funds and accounts as may be designated, or so much thereof as
58 may be necessary, and the total amount to be expended for the
59 items for which the appropriation is herein made shall not
60 exceed the amount provided therefor, except as provided in the
61 Budget Management Act of 1976, Sections 41-19-1 through
62 41-19-12, Code of Alabama 1975. Provided, however, that
63 regardless of the ending date of any pay period which has been
64 or may be established by the Legislature for the payment of
65 salaries of state employees, the entire payment due shall be
66 made from the fiscal year's appropriation in which the pay
67 date falls.
68 (b) All appropriations made in Section 3 shall be at
69 the program level. Any directed expenditure of funds below a
70 program shall be from funds appropriated for the program.
Page 3

program shall be from funds appropriated for the program.

State General
Fund Other Funds Total
296 In addition to the above appropriation herein made, there is hereby appropriated for
297 each additional retail and wholesale store that is relocated or put into operation
298 during the fiscal year, an amount equal to the sum required to install and operate a
299 comparable store in operation by said Board. There is further appropriated to the
300 Alabama Alcoholic Beverage Control Board, after provision has been made for the
301 other expenditures herein authorized, such sums as are or may be necessary to
302 purchase the alcoholic beverages which are essential to maintain adequate stocks and
303 inventory for an economic and successful sales operation. In addition to the above
304 appropriation, it is further provided that, in the event any county or municipality
305 of the state shall, during the fiscal period covered by this appropriation by proper
306 referendum, authorize the legal sale of malt and brewed beverages within such county
307 or municipality there is further appropriated, in addition to the amount herein set
308 out, an amount comparable to that expended during the prior fiscal year for beer and
309 license tax supervision within counties or municipalities of similar size and
310 population. Provided further, that the amount appropriated herein shall be reduced
311 in like manner in the event any county or municipality wherein malt and brewed
312 beverages are now authorized by law to be sold shall, during the fiscal period
313 covered by this appropriation by proper referendum, declare unlawful the sale in
314 such county or municipality of such malt or brewed beverages. Notwithstanding any
315 other laws to the contrary, all revenue generated from bailment fees shall remain
316 with the Board to be used for its operations.

1255 61. Health, Department of Public:

1258 (1) Office of Primary Care and Rural 500,000
1259 Health
1260 For award payments to licensed physicians or nurse practitioners who agree to practice
1261 full-time in primary care in a medically underserved rural area for an agreed upon number of
1262 years. No payment shall be allowed for a physician or nurse practitioner who has practiced
1263 within three years of October 1, 2026, in a primary care service area with a deficit, or
1264 surplus of less than 2.0 primary-care physicians, as shown by the most-recent Status Report of
1265 the Alabama Primary Care Physician Workforce from the Office for Family Health Education &
1266 Research at the UAB Huntsville Regional Medical Campus. The Office of Primary Care and Rural
1267 Health may pay an eligible physician or nurse practitioner as much as $50,000 a year for each
1268 year of service, in a medically underserved rural area, agreed to by contract by the physician
1269 or nurse practitioner, but any payment shall be for no more than three years. Contracts shall
1270 set out refund and penalty requirements for failure by a physician or nurse practitioner to
1271 meet the contract terms. A medically underserved rural area as determined by the Office shall
1272 be: (1.) in a rural primary care service area with a deficit of primary-care physicians as
1273 shown by the most recent Status Report of the Alabama Primary Care Physician Workforce, and
1274 (2.) in a county in which no more than two physicians have worked or are scheduled to be
1275 working within 12 months to repay a loan awarded by the Alabama Board of Medical Scholarship
1276 Awards. The Office shall file a report with the Chairs of the Senate Committee on Finance and
1277 Taxation-General Fund and the House Ways and Means-General Fund Committee, the Legislative
1278 Fiscal Officer and the Finance Director by October 15, 2027, on how the money was spent in
1279 fiscal year 2027 and the names of participants and where they agreed to practice or were
1280 practicing in return for payments from the Office.

1314 To award matching grants for ambulances for emergency medical services operating in rural
1315 counties. The Office may consider requests for matching grants to buy an ambulance,
1316 rapid-response vehicle, or cardiac monitor or other durable medical equipment to be placed in
1317 an ambulance or rapid-response vehicle, from a county, city, hospital, or ambulance service.
1318 The Office may award a grant equal to no more than 75 percent of the cost of the ambulance,
1319 rapid-response vehicle, or equipment, the percentage depending on the financial resources of
1320 the applicant and the need for the vehicle or equipment as judged by officials with the state’s
1321 regional emergency medical services offices. Preference shall be given to grants for an
1322 ambulance or rapid-response vehicle that would be based in a county with two or fewer

1756 84. Medicaid Agency, Alabama:
1757 (a) Medical Assistance through 1,179,054,000 9,338,373,438 10,517,427,438
1758 Medicaid Program
1759 The Medicaid Agency shall make every effort to maintain level funding for the
1760 adult prosthetic and orthotic program in fiscal year 2027. Any requirements
1761 for prior authorization of antipsychotic drugs will be for the limited purpose
1762 of managing off-label utilization. The Medicaid Agency shall make every effort
1763 to provide access for medications prescribed in accordance with FDA approved
1764 indications for mental illness and HIV/AIDS. The Alabama Medicaid Agency shall
1765 not pay for a generic drug that is more expensive than its brand name drug,
1766 net of rebates. The Alabama Medicaid Agency shall continue to fund and support
1767 the PACE program in accordance with written agreements.

2455 Total Revenue, Department of 363,000 229,166,353 229,529,353
2456 The amounts hereinabove appropriated for the cost of maintenance and operations of
2457 the Department of Revenue are in lieu of any other statutory provisions for the
2458 payment of the cost of operating said Department for collections of the taxes as
2459 authorized by law. Provided, however, in addition to the amount hereinabove
2460 appropriated, there is hereby appropriated to the Department of Revenue all sums
2461 allowed the Department of Revenue by acts of the Legislature as a charge for the
2462 collection of taxes or licenses. The Revenue Department shall not be limited in any
2463 way whatsoever in its ability to utilize or spend its full appropriation and all
2464 sums allowed to the Department of Revenue by acts of the Legislature as a charge for
2465 the collection of taxes or licenses. It is the intent of the Legislature that the
2466 Department of Revenue utilize the appropriations made to it in this act to: (1)
2467 significantly reduce the amount of delinquent taxes owed to the state; (2) employ
2468 sufficient examiners and audit personnel to ensure that taxes owed to the state are
2469 collected accurately and timely; and (3) update its personal computers and related
2470 equipment to become more efficient in the collection of taxes owed to the state.
2471 During Fiscal Year 2027, the Department shall report semi-annually to the Chairs of
2472 the House Ways and Means-General Fund Committee, Senate Finance and Taxation-General
2473 Fund Committee, and the Legislative Fiscal Officer on all actions taken by the
2474 Department in furtherance of these goals. The reports shall include, but not be
2475 limited to: (1) the number and amount of delinquent taxes collected during the
2476 quarter and the number and amounts of delinquent taxes outstanding as of the end of
2477 the quarter; (2) the number of additional examiners and audit personnel employed
2478 during the quarter (not including examiners and audit personnel employed to replace
2479 personnel that retire or otherwise leave state service); and (3) the number of new
2480 personal computers and related equipment put into use during the quarter.

2528 The Alabama SenioRx program shall provide assistance obtaining prescription
2529 medications and shall be expanded to allow comprehensive benefits screening
2530 and application assistance through an Area Agency on Aging designated by the
2531 Department as an Aging and Disability Resource Center (ADRC). It is the intent
2532 of the Legislature that applicants apply through local Area Agencies on Aging
2533 and their provider networks to ensure services are maximized and that
2534 paperwork and inconvenience to the clients are minimized to receive access to
2535 local and public benefits and prescription assistance. The Department of
2536 Senior Services shall report semi-annually to the Chairs of the House Ways and
2537 Means-General Fund Committee and the Senate Finance and Taxation-General Fund
2538 Committee, the Governor, the Director of Finance, and the Legislative Fiscal
2539 Officer. The reports shall include the number of clients served by an ADRC,
2540 the number of unduplicated SenioRx participants, the number of prescriptions
2541 filled, and the estimated value of the drugs provided.

3206 Section 4. In addition to the amounts otherwise
3207 appropriated in this act, there is hereby appropriated from
3208 the several funds in the State Treasury, except the Education
3209 Trust Fund, and in the same proportion as the salaries of the
3210 several State officials and employees are paid, such
3211 additional amounts as may be necessary to pay for a two
3212 percent (2%) salary increase enacted in the 2026 Regular
3213 Session. The additional amounts appropriated in this section
3214 from the State General Fund shall not exceed $16,000,000 for
3215 the fiscal year ending September 30, 2027. The Director of
3216 Finance shall ensure that first priority shall be given to all
3217 State General Fund payrolls, including the payroll of the
3218 Legislature. State agencies shall receive additional
3219 allocations from the appropriation made in this section from
3220 the State General Fund in amounts necessary to increase total
3221 salaries paid from the State General Fund by two percent. The
3222 remainder of this appropriation from the State General Fund
3223 may be allotted by the Director of Finance to those agencies
3224 which receive transfers from the State General Fund.
